<p>The <b>State University of New York at Buffalo</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> with campuses in <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York">Amherst</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, United States. It is commonly referred to as the <b>University at Buffalo</b> (<b>UB</b>) or <b>SUNY Buffalo</b>, and it was formerly known as the <b>University of Buffalo</b>. The university was founded in 1846 as a private college, but in 1962 merged with the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> (SUNY) system. By enrollment, UB is the largest in the SUNY system,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and also the largest public university in the northeastern United States (consisting of New York state and the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> region). UB also has the largest endowment and research funding, as a comprehensive university center in the SUNY system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the university enrolls 29,806 students<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buffalo.edu_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-buffalo.edu-1">[1]</a></sup> in 13 colleges. In addition to the College of Arts and Sciences, the university houses the largest state-operated <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_school" title="Dental school">dental school</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_school" title="Education school">education school</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_school" title="Business school">business school</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engineering_school" title="Engineering school">engineering school</a>, and also features the only state <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law school</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a> school, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a> school in the state of New York. The university offers over 100 bachelor's, 205 master's, 84 doctoral, and 10 professional areas of study.</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>, the University at Buffalo is a Doctoral University with the Highest research activity (R1).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1989, UB was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, which represents 62 prestigious, leading research universities in the United States and Canada. UB's alumni and faculty have included a <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Abdullahi_Mohamed" title="Mohamed Abdullahi Mohamed">Prime Minister</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronauts" title="Astronauts">astronauts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" title="Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billionaires" title="Billionaires">billionaires</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> winners, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fulbright_Scholars" title="Fulbright Scholars">Fulbright Scholars</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars">Rhodes Scholars</a>. The university was founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._President" title="U.S. President">U.S. President</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Vice_President" title="U.S. Vice President">U.S. Vice President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>, who served as the school's first chancellor, making UB one of the only two universities founded by a U.S. President.</p>
<p>In the Wall Street Journal/Times Higher Education 2017 inaugural ranking, UB was ranked as the #1 public university in New York and #28 in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Buffalo has consistently placed in the top cluster of U.S. public research universities and among the overall top 30 research universities according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance-10">[10]</a></sup> and was ranked as the 38th best value for in-state students and the 27th best value for out-of-state students in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a> rankings of best value of national universities. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2017 edition of America's Best Colleges ranked UB 99th on their list of best national universities and 43rd among public universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy,_1857.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1861" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/170px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/255px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/340px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy,_1857.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Official White House portrait of <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>City leaders of Buffalo sought to establish a university in the city from the earliest days of Buffalo. A <b>University of Western New York</b> was begun at Buffalo under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/United_Presbyterian_Church_in_the_United_States_of_America" title="United Presbyterian Church in the United States of America">Presbyterian Church</a> and property was purchased at North Street and College, (the site of the later YMCA), on the north side of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allentown,_Buffalo,_New_York" title="Allentown, Buffalo, New York">Allentown district</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-12">[12]</a></sup> This university was chartered by the state on April 8, 1836. However, the project collapsed and no classes were ever offered, and only the layout of College Street remains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b>University of Buffalo</b> was founded by United States President <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> on May 11, 1846,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-12">[12]</a></sup> prior to his ascension to the presidency, as a private medical school to train the doctors for the communities of <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_New_York" title="Niagara Falls, New York">Niagara Falls</a>, and surrounding villages. James Platt White was instrumental in obtaining a charter for the University of Buffalo from the state legislature in 1846. He also taught the first class of 89 men in obstetrics. State Assemblyman <a href="/wiki/Nathan_K._Hall" title="Nathan K. Hall">Nathan K. Hall</a> was also "particularly active in procuring the charter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-14">[14]</a></sup> The doors first opened to students in 1847 and after associating with a hospital for teaching purposes, the first class of students graduated the medical school in July 1847. Founder Millard Fillmore served as the school's first chancellor. Upon his ascension to the presidency after <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">President Taylor's</a> death, Fillmore stayed on as part-time chancellor. Fillmore's name now graces the continuing education school Millard Fillmore College on the South campus as well as the Millard Fillmore Academic Center, an academic and administrative services building at the core of the residential Joseph Ellicott Complex, on the North Campus.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="800" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/270px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/405px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/540px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg 2x" width="270"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1907 Pub Scene, students singing</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"The first lectures were delivered in a wooden building over the old post office, corner of Seneca and Washington streets."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-14">[14]</a></sup> The first building specially built for the university was a stone building at the corner of Main and Virginia streets, built in 1849–50, through donations, public subscription, and a state grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough2_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-14">[14]</a></sup> There were continuous expansions to the college medical programs, including a separate pharmacy division, which is now The School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences. In 1887, a law school was organized in Buffalo, which quickly became associated with <a href="/wiki/Niagara_University" title="Niagara University">Niagara University</a> just to the north of Buffalo. After four years, in 1891, the law school was acquired by the University of Buffalo as the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">University of Buffalo Law School</a>, which had a downtown Buffalo facility. In the first few years of the 20th century, the University began planning for a comprehensive undergraduate college to complete the basic structure of a university, and in 1909 the University acquired the Erie County Almshouse grounds from the county of Erie, which became the University of Buffalo's initial campus. The establishment may have been influenced by the 1910 <a href="/wiki/Flexner_Report" title="Flexner Report">Flexner Report</a> which criticized the preparation of the medical students at the university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Why_Innovation_Fails_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Innovation_Fails-15">[15]</a></sup> With that additional space, in 1915, the then University of Buffalo formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_College_of_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo College of Arts &amp; Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a>, creating an undergraduate division in addition to its prior educational work in the licensed professional fields. In 1916, Grace Millard Knox pledged $500,000 for the establishment of a "department of liberal arts and sciences in the University of Buffalo", which was at the time still a private institution. The initial gift of $100,000 was for the purchase of what would become Townsend Hall and the remainder was to establish the university's first endowment, in her husband's name, to support the department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_History_of_the_University_of_Buffalo_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-A_History_of_the_University_of_Buffalo-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="322" data-file-width="254" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png/170px-Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/83/Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
First home of the Medical College</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1950, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_Engineering" title="Industrial Engineering">Industrial Engineering</a> department branched off from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_Engineering" title="Mechanical Engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a> department. In 1956, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Engineering" title="Civil Engineering">Civil Engineering</a> Department was formed under <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_University" title="Lehigh University">Lehigh University</a> graduate <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Ketter" title="Robert L. Ketter">Robert L. Ketter</a>, who went on to become Dean of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, and later President of the University. In 1959, <a href="/wiki/WBFO" title="WBFO">WBFO</a> was launched as an AM radio station by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">UB's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, and run by UB's students. The station has since become the launching pad of two modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a> personalities: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terri_Gross" title="Terri Gross">Terri Gross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ira_Flatow" title="Ira Flatow">Ira Flatow</a>. In 1961, the Western New York nuclear research program was created. This program installed a miniature, active nuclear fission reactor on the University's South (Main Street) Campus. This program was not particularly active, nor could it compete with other government-run research labs, consequently, the programs performed in this facility were abandoned somewhat shortly after its inception. This reactor was decommissioned in 2005 with little fanfare due to material security concerns.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_by_the_SUNY_system_and_second_campus">Acquisition by the SUNY system and second campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acquisition by the SUNY system and second campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1962, the private University of Buffalo was purchased by and incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> or SUNY system, and became known as the <b>State University of New York at Buffalo</b>. As a part of the agreement to merge the university into the SUNY system, the State began to build an extensive second campus for the university. In 1964, The State acquired several hundred acres in the town of <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York">Amherst</a> on the northeast of Buffalo, for development as a comprehensive campus for most of the non-medical disciplines at the University at Buffalo. This is often called the North Campus, and the center of most University at Buffalo activities. The North Campus project included several major buildings, dormitory complexes, a separate spur of the Interstate highway, and a new lake. The undergraduate college, the law school, and graduate schools were all moved to the new campus. During the late 1960s, the College of Arts and Sciences was divided into three separate schools: arts and letters, natural sciences and mathematics, and social sciences. During the 1998–1999 academic year, the three schools were reunited to re-create the existing College of Arts and Sciences, when the faculties of Arts &amp; Letters, Social Sciences, and Natural Sciences and Mathematics were combined, according to a memorandum issued by the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SUNY_memo_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-SUNY_memo-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="UB_2020">UB 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: UB 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Started in 2004 under President John B. Simpson, UB 2020 is a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_planning" title="Strategic planning">strategic planning</a> initiative to develop and implement a vision for the university over the next 15 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-overview-18">[18]</a></sup> The centerpiece of UB 2020 is to add about 10,000 more students, 750 faculty members and 600 staff, increasing the size of the university by about 40 percent. UB 2020 also recognizes the university's contribution to the surrounding region. The most recent estimates of UB's impact on the local and regional economies of Western New York report approximately $1.7 billion are brought into the local economy from the presence of UB. This figure is also expected to rise by 40 percent, corresponding with UB's institutional growth.</p>
<p>One of the keys to helping UB achieve the goals of the UB 2020 plan, proponents say, is the passage of S2020 and A2020 known as the UB 2020 Flexibility and Economic Growth Act, by the New York State Legislature. On June 3, 2009, the State Senate passed S2020 and sent the bill to the Assembly for their consideration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="424" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png/250px-UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png/375px-UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UB_Student_Introduces_Obama.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A UB student, Silvana D'Ettorre, introduced President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> at a speech given in <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Arena_(University_at_Buffalo)" title="Alumni Arena (University at Buffalo)">Alumni Arena</a> in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The current president, <a href="/wiki/Satish_K._Tripathi" title="Satish K. Tripathi">Satish K. Tripathi</a>, has continued his vocal support of UB 2020<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ub_2020_overview_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-ub_2020_overview-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-president_ub_2020_overview_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-president_ub_2020_overview-21">[21]</a></sup> and has been actively engaging in campus-wide discussion on the proposed tuition increases introduced by the bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_Senate_bill_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Senate_bill-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, the School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences received an anonymous donation of $40 million from an alumnus who had graduated from the university during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WGRZ_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-WGRZ-23">[23]</a></sup> The donation will contribute to the $375 million project which will relocate the School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences to UB's downtown campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UB_Reporter_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-UB_Reporter-24">[24]</a></sup> The new school will be designed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HOK_Architects" title="HOK Architects">HOK Architects</a>.</p>
<p>From FY2011 to FY2012, UB had spent over $300 million on the strategic plan to construct and open four new buildings, including <a href="/wiki/Barbara_and_Jack_Davis_Hall" title="Barbara and Jack Davis Hall">Davis Hall</a>, William R. Greiner Residence Hall, the Clinical and Translational Research Center and Kaleida Health medical research building, and Crossroads Culinary Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_Hall_Opening_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis_Hall_Opening-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 22, 2013, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> came to UB's campus to give a speech about needed higher education reform in the country. President Obama highlighted UB's accolades and specifically chose Buffalo for its excellence and commitment to the future, graduation rates and retention, and quality education at an affordable price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015 the UB 2020 initiative, Heart of the Campus will be implemented on each of UB's three campuses in phases. The new school of medicine is also being constructed with additional funding from the NYSUNY 2020 legislation and from a donation of $30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The university's official legal name is "State University of New York at Buffalo". The formal academic and more commonly used name is "University at Buffalo", informally "UB". This name is similar to the university's former name of over a 100 years, "University of Buffalo". The "University at Buffalo, The State University of New York" is a secondary academic name with SUNY present that is used less often. Other names like "SUNY at Buffalo" and "Buffalo" are also commonly seen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The university's athletic department, particularly on uniforms use the name "Buffalo".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_organization">Administration and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administration and organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/220px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/330px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/440px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clark Hall on UB's South Campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Buffalo is a public university and is one of four university centers of the 64 campuses in the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> (SUNY) which enrolled 467,991 students and employed 88,024 academic staff in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SUNY_Fast_Facts_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-SUNY_Fast_Facts-33">[33]</a></sup> SUNY is governed by a 17-member Board of Trustees, 15 of whom are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a> and the remaining two members being elected from the Student Assembly and University Faculty Senate. <a href="/wiki/Carl_McCall" title="Carl McCall">Carl McCall</a> is the Chairman of the SUNY Board of Trustees and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_L._Zimpher" title="Nancy L. Zimpher">Nancy L. Zimpher</a> is the Chancellor of the SUNY system. <a href="/wiki/Satish_K._Tripathi" title="Satish K. Tripathi">Satish K. Tripathi</a> was appointed by the SUNY Board of Trustees as the 15th president of the University at Buffalo in April 2011 after previously serving a six-year tenure as the UB provost and executive vice president for academic affairs. He receives compensation of $385,000, $115,000, and $150,000 annually from each of the university, SUNY Research Foundation, and the UB Foundation respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The University at Buffalo Foundation (UB Foundation) was chartered in 1962 as an independent non-profit corporation and is controlled by a privately appointed board of trustees. It serves as a vehicle to raise private funds for the university, develop real estate, and manage endowment investments on behalf of the university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The foundation managed a $685.2 million endowment for FY2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>UB is organized into 13 academic schools and colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>School of Architecture and Planning</b> is the only combined architecture and urban planning school in the State University of New York system and offers the only accredited professional master's degree in architecture and is one of two SUNY schools that offers an accredited professional master's degree in urban planning. In addition, the Buffalo School of Architecture and Planning also awards the original undergraduate four year pre-professional degrees in architecture and environmental design in the SUNY system. Other degree programs offered by the Buffalo School of Architecture and Planning include a research oriented Master of Science in Architecture with specializations in historic preservation/urban design, inclusive design, and computing and media technologies; a PhD in urban and regional planning; and, an advanced graduate certificate in historic preservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>College of Arts and Sciences</b> was founded in 1915 and is the largest and most comprehensive academic unit at UB with 25 academic departments, 12 academic programs, and 21 centers and institutes across the humanities, arts, and sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-General_Information_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-General_Information-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Buffalo_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="State University of New York at Buffalo School of Dental Medicine">School of Dental Medicine</a></b> was founded in 1892 and offers accredited programs in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Dental_Surgery" title="Doctor of Dental Surgery">DDS</a>, oral surgery, and other oral sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>Graduate School of Education</b> was founded in 1931 and is one of the largest graduate schools at UB. The school has four academic departments: counseling and educational psychology, educational leadership and policy, learning and instruction, and library and information science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In academic year 2008–2009, the Graduate School of Education awarded 472 master's degrees and 52 doctoral degrees.</li>
<li>The <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a></b> was founded in 1946 and offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in six departments. It is the largest public school of engineering in the state of New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">School of Law</a></b> was founded in 1887 and is the only law school in the SUNY system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The school awarded 265 JD degrees in the 2009–2010 academic year.</li>
<li>The <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Buffalo_School_of_Management" title="State University of New York at Buffalo School of Management">School of Management</a></b> was founded in 1923 and offers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AACSB" title="AACSB">AACSB</a>-accredited undergraduate, MBA, and doctoral degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_School_of_Medicine_and_Biomedical_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences">School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences</a></b> is the founding faculty of the UB and began in 1846. It offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in the biomedical and biotechnical sciences as well as a MD program and residencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>School of Nursing</b> was founded in 1936 and offers bachelors, masters, and doctoral degrees in nursing practice and patient care.</li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_School_of_Pharmacy_and_Pharmaceutical_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences">School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences</a></b> was founded in 1886, making it the second-oldest faculty at UB and the only pharmacy school in the SUNY system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>School of Public Health and Health Professions</b> was founded in 2003 from the merger of the Department of Social and Preventive Medicine and the UB School of Health Related Professions. The school offers a bachelor's degree in exercise science as well as professional, master's and PhD degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <b>School of Social Work</b> offers graduate <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Social_Work" title="Master of Social Work">MSW</a> and doctoral degrees in <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social work</a>.</li>
<li>The <b>Roswell Park Graduate Division</b> is an affiliated academic unit within the Graduate School of UB, in partnership with <b><a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a></b>, an independent NCI-designated Comprehensive Cancer Center. The Roswell Park Graduate Division offers five PhD programs and two MS programs in basic and translational biomedical research related to cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Roswell Park Cancer Institute was founded in 1898 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Roswell_Park" title="Dr. Roswell Park">Dr. Roswell Park</a> and was the world's first cancer research institute.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parker_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/220px-Parker_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/330px-Parker_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/440px-Parker_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parker_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Parker Hall, home to Millard Fillmore College<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>University at Buffalo is a large, public research university with very high research activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carnegie_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-50">[50]</a></sup> The university has been accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Commission_on_Higher_Education" title="Middle States Commission on Higher Education">Middle States Commission on Higher Education</a> since 1921.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 2009, the university awarded 4,036 bachelor's degrees across 74 undergraduate programs, 2,076 master's degree across 190 programs, 367 doctoral degrees across 83 programs, and 609 professional degrees across 18 programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The State University of New York at Buffalo is often referred to as New York's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagship_university" title="Flagship university">public flagship university</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buffalo.edu_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-buffalo.edu-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ubbulls.com_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-ubbulls.com-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-College_board_2014_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-College_board_2014-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washingtonpost.com_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Washingtonpost.com-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campus_Watch_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campus_Watch-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[note 1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The four-year, full-time undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments at the university which emphasizes a balanced curriculum across the arts, sciences, and professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carnegie_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-50">[50]</a></sup> The university enrolled 19,951 undergraduate and 9,855 graduate students in the fall of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enrollments_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-69">[68]</a></sup> Women make up 48% of the student body and 78% of the student body is from the state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UnivProfile_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-UnivProfile-70">[69]</a></sup> 7,204 students live on-campus, 10,172 students live off campus, and 11,505 students commute; Despite this strikingly high number of commuters, over 70% of students live on campus their first year. Note: The term "off campus" includes students who live in the residential apartments within the campus perimeter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UnivProfile_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-UnivProfile-70">[69]</a></sup> Undergraduate tuition, room &amp; board, and fees for New York state residents for the 2011–2012 school year totals $18,681 and costs to out-of-state residents totals $27,461.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="720" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/220px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/330px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/440px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UB's Health and Sciences Library, Abbott Hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Emphasis has been placed on developing a community of research scientists centered around an economic initiative to promote Buffalo and create the Center of Excellence for Bioinformatics and Life Sciences as well as other advanced biomedical and engineering disciplines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Total R&amp;D for the fiscal year of 2013 was at $360 million, ranking 61st, which is higher than that of <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts</a>, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> UB offered an early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_Science" title="Computer Science">Computer Science</a> major (distinct from a mathematics major).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Additionally, UB played a significant role as a crucial internet hub for the eastern seaboard during the internet's inception.</p>
<p>University at Buffalo academic and professional faculty are represented by United University Professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The two UUP chapters at the University at Buffalo are Health Sciences and Buffalo Center. United University Professions has over 34,000 members at 29 campuses of SUNY.</p>
<p>The University at Buffalo is also one of only two public schools in New York to have a medical school and a dental school, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_University" title="Stony Brook University">Stony Brook University</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UB's admission is selective with high levels of transfer-in as well as rolling admission deadlines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carnegie_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-50">[50]</a></sup> The university received 21,985 applications for the Class of 2015, admitted 11,298 (51.4%), and matriculated 3,154 (27.9%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDS_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-76">[75]</a></sup> Among first year students, 35% graduated in the top tenth of their high school class<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freshman_Admission_Criteria_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Admission_Criteria-77">[76]</a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter-quartile_range" title="Inter-quartile range">inter-quartile range</a> was 500–610 for SAT reading, 550–650 for SAT math, and 24–29 on the ACT composite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDS_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-76">[75]</a></sup> The class of 2014 included over 900 merit scholars and 320 honors college students. Within the honors college, the average combined math and reading SAT score was 1382, which was higher than the average SAT score of students admitted to <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>, and high school grade average for the incoming class was 97%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Admissions_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Admissions-78">[77]</a></sup> UB received 6,107 transfer applicants, admitted 3,623, and enrolled 1,850.</p>

<p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2017 edition of America's Best Colleges ranked UB 99th on their list of "Best National Universities", and 43rd among public universities. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> (EPA) ranks UB 1st on their "Green Power List" of top colleges and universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> In the Wall Street Journal/Times Higher Education 2017 inaugural ranking of top colleges and universities, the University at Buffalo was ranked as the 1st best public university in New York and 28th best in the nation <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a> is ranked 63rd. The <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_School_of_Management" title="University at Buffalo School of Management">School of Management</a> is ranked 77th by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News" title="U.S. News">U.S. News</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> 45th by <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> and 60th by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a>, making UB the highest ranked public business school in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The School of Education at UB is well regarded, and is ranked 71st. The School of Public Health and Health Professions is ranked 31st, the School of Nursing is ranked 75th for masters, 38th for doctorate, with the anesthesia program ranking 10th in the nation. The <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_School_of_Pharmacy_and_Pharmaceutical_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences">School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences</a> is ranked 22nd, the School of Social Work is ranked 27th, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUNY_Buffalo_Law_School" title="SUNY Buffalo Law School">School of law</a> is ranked 100th. UB was ranked the 64th best college for veterans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The audiology program is ranked 17th, rehabilitation counseling is ranked 21st, speech-language pathology is ranked 30th, English is ranked 44th, library and information studies is ranked 39th, math is 73rd, physics is 85th, fine arts is 69th, political science is 76th, history is 92nd, physical therapy is 79th, occupational therapy is 32nd, computer science is 63rd, chemistry is 76th, statistics is 70th, psychology is 63rd, and clinical psychology is ranked 50th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>U.S News ranking of best online programs ranks UB 21st in "Best Online Bachelor's Programs" and 10th in "Best Online Graduate Education Programs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_97-3"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/220px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/330px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/440px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historic Foster Hall on UB's South Campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 2015–2016 edition of "World University Rankings", <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> ranked UB at 191. US News and Report ranked the university 181 on their "Best Global Universities" ranking. College magazine ranked SUNY Buffalo #4 in the "best campuses for out-of-state students".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a>'s "Best Values in Public Colleges" of 2012, the University at Buffalo ranks 38th in the nation for in-state students and 27th in the nation for out-of-state students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> In 2015, SUNY Buffalo was ranked #15 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State" title="New York State">New York State</a> by average professor salaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">University at Buffalo Libraries</a></div>
<p>UB has nine libraries on its North (Amherst), South (Buffalo), and Downtown (Buffalo) campuses. The libraries' 3.8 million-plus print volumes are augmented by extensive digital resources, including full-text electronic journals, databases, media, and special collections, which include the world's single largest collection of James Joyce manuscripts and artifacts.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The University at Buffalo is the state's largest and most comprehensive public university and is spread across three campuses: North Campus, South Campus, and Downtown Campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> The Sustainable Endowments Institute's College Sustainability Report Card awarded the university a B+.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> UB was awarded the EPA "Environmental Champion Award" in 2015 and is ranked as one of the top 50 "green colleges and universities" in the nation, working towards becoming climate neutral by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Campus">North Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: North Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The North Campus, a <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated place</a> also called "University at Buffalo", located in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York"><b>Amherst</b></a>, began in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haar_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haar-110">[109]</a></sup> Many academic programs, including the entirety of the undergraduate College of Arts and Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">University at Buffalo Law School</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, the School of Management, the Graduate School of Social Work, and the Graduate School of Education, as well as <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries#Lockwood_Memorial_Library" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">Lockwood Memorial Library</a>, Capen Library, and many administrative offices, are located on UB's North Campus.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg/220px-O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg/330px-O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg/440px-O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:O%27Brian_Hall_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
O'Brian Hall, home to the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">School of Law</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The North Campus is home to administrative and academic offices. The main buildings are arranged along one academic "spine", a second floor connecting corridor, that connects most of the main academic buildings. The whole campus covers 1,192 acres (5 km<sup>2</sup>) with 146 buildings containing 6,715,492 sq ft (623,890 m<sup>2</sup>), 10 residence halls and 5 apartment complexes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-106">[105]</a></sup> Its immense size also necessitated the creation of a shuttle system circling the academic sector and surrounding areas including the administrative complex, located nearly a quarter mile from the central academic area. When originally built by the state of New York, the North Campus was provided with two Interstate exits, from <a href="/wiki/Interstate_290_(New_York)" title="Interstate 290 (New York)">I-290</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_990_(New_York)" title="Interstate 990 (New York)">I-990</a>, its own internal parkway, the John James Audubon Parkway, and two small lakes created from <a href="/wiki/Ellicott_Creek" title="Ellicott Creek">Ellicott Creek</a>. As a census-designated place, the residential population recorded at the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a> was 6,066.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2010_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The North Campus offers a variety of entertainment programming and activity for students. It contains the Student Union, which houses offices for the Student Association and student-interest clubs; Slee Hall, which presents contemporary and classical music concerts; <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Arena_(University_at_Buffalo)" title="Alumni Arena (University at Buffalo)">Alumni Arena</a>, the home-court for University Athletics; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UB_Center_for_the_Arts" title="UB Center for the Arts">UB Center for the Arts</a>, a non-profit presenter of a wide variety of professional entertainment and <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Stadium" title="University at Buffalo Stadium">University at Buffalo Stadium</a>, the 30,000 seat <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> stadium.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Campus">South Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: South Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="796" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/220px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/330px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/440px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Overlooking UB's South Campus from Abbott Hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The South Campus, also known as the Main Street campus, located on 154 acres (0.62 km<sup>2</sup>) in North Buffalo, is the former grounds of the Erie County Almshouse and Insane Asylum, of which four buildings still remain (Hayes Hall, the former insane asylum; Wende Hall, a former maternity hospital; Hayes D; and Townsend Hall, a former nurses' quarters).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> The college was designed by architect E.B. Green in 1910, and was intended to resemble <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Dublin" title="Trinity College, Dublin">Trinity College, Dublin</a>. Its 53 buildings contain (3,045,198 sq ft (282,908 m<sup>2</sup>)) and include six resident halls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-106">[105]</a></sup> This campus is served by the northernmost <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_(Metro_Rail)" title="University (Metro Rail)">subway station</a> on Buffalo's Niagara Frontier <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Metro_Rail" title="Buffalo Metro Rail">Metro Rail</a> system.</p>
<p>Today, the South Campus is home to the School of Pharmacy, Dental School, and the School of Architecture and Urban Planning. The Medical School is currently in the process of moving from South Campus to the new Downtown Campus in Buffalo. In addition, the University at Buffalo South Campus is the home of the <a href="/wiki/WBFO" title="WBFO">WBFO</a> radio station, the University's biomedical science research complex, the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries#Health_Sciences_Library" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">Health Sciences Library</a>, and certain administrative offices. 20 percent of UB's resident population also continues to live in the original residential complexes located on the South (Main Street) Campus.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_Campus">Downtown Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Downtown Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, UB commissioned Boston firm Chan Krieger to create a third campus center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haar_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haar-110">[109]</a></sup> The Downtown Campus is the site of UB's New York State Center of Excellence in Bioinformatics and Life Science, which partners in research with UB's Ira G. Ross Eye Institute<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hauptman-Woodward_Medical_Research_Institute" title="Hauptman-Woodward Medical Research Institute">Hauptman-Woodward Medical Research Institute</a> to compose the Buffalo-Niagara Medical Campus. The medical campus, which is designed to meet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LEED_Silver" title="LEED Silver">LEED Silver</a> criteria, incorporates high efficiency lighting, heat recovery systems, and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EnergyStar" title="EnergyStar">EnergyStar</a> roof.</p>
<p>Also located in the downtown area is UB's Research Institute on Addictions (RIA), Educational Opportunity Center (EOC)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> and the Jacobs Executive Development Center (JEDC). The campus includes six major properties and a total of 43 buildings, counting shared lease space (588,506 sq ft (54,674 m<sup>2</sup>)).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2007, UB added the former <a href="/wiki/M._Wile_and_Company_Factory_Building" title="M. Wile and Company Factory Building">M. Wile and Company Factory Building</a> on the southeast corner of Goodell and Ellicott streets and the former <a href="/wiki/Trico_Plant_No._1" title="Trico Plant No. 1">Trico Products Corp. building complex</a> on the northwest corner of Goodell and Ellicott streets to its properties downtown. The UB Regional Institute, Center on Rehabilitation Synergy, and a number of pre-K-16 initiatives related to UB's civic engagement mission, such as the UB-Buffalo Public Schools Partnership office, are set to relocate to the first site. The latter location has been purchased to house additional biomedical- and life science-related businesses connected to the Buffalo-Niagara Medical Campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching_hospitals">Teaching hospitals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Teaching hospitals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>UB's teaching hospitals include Buffalo General Hospital, the Erie County Medical Center (ECMC), Millard Fillmore Hospital, Roswell Park Cancer Institute and Veterans Affairs Western New York Health Care System. Additional facilities include free clinics such as the Kaleida Health's Niagara Family Health Center and the Lighthouse Free Medical Clinic, a program run by UB medical students.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UB_art_galleries">UB art galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: UB art galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_university_art_museums_and_galleries_in_New_York_State" title="List of university art museums and galleries in New York State">List of university art museums and galleries in New York State</a></div>
<p>UB is home to two university art galleries, the <b>UB Anderson Art Gallery</b> and the <b>UB Art Gallery at the Center for the Arts</b>. Adjacent to the UB South Campus is the UB Anderson Art Gallery,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> a converted elementary school with an all-glass atrium exhibit space. The UB Anderson Gallery hosts exhibitions curated by faculty and visiting curators and features works from international and professional artist in its two floor facility. The UB Anderson Gallery building, along with over 1,200 works of art, was donated to the University in 2000 by collector and gallery owner David K. Anderson, son of legendary New York gallerist Martha Jackson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> Selections from the personal collection of Martha Jackson that was donated to the UB Anderson Gallery by David Anderson are on display in a 360 degree permanent installation in the <b>Martha Jackson Gallery Archives and Research Center</b>, on the second floor of the gallery.</p>
<p>The UB Art Gallery at the Center for the Arts is located on the north campus, and features works from contemporary artists, as well as faculty and students across disciplines.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comprehensive_Physical_Plan">Comprehensive Physical Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Comprehensive Physical Plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The University at Buffalo has grown to an enrollment of approximately 30,000 undergraduate and <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">graduate students</a>, and a staff of 14,000 employees, across three campuses in the last 160 years. In order to accommodate both students and faculty, the university is currently implementing a $4.5 million Comprehensive Physical Plan to help in growth as well as to best utilize and enhance current facilities. Connecting all three campuses, as well as the facilities UB uses, is also a major element of the project. The firm granted the contract to lead the project is <a href="/wiki/Beyer_Blinder_Belle" title="Beyer Blinder Belle">Beyer Blinder Belle</a>.</p>
<p>The comprehensive physical planning process is broken into four phases. Currently, UB is implementing "phase one" by seeking input from the local and university communities to pinpoint issues, opportunities, and concerns related to this expansion. The project recognizes UB's potential for excellence, in regard to the university's physical environment, by highlighting and evaluating various positive and negative attributes of the three campuses, including housing, circulation, functionality, landscape, and community interface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Campus_gallery">South Campus gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: South Campus gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
