<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associations_and_activities">Associations and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Associations and activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UB has two student-run periodicals: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectrum_(newspaper)" title="The Spectrum (newspaper)">The Spectrum</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Generation_Magazine" title="Generation Magazine">Generation</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> Both publications are distributed on campus. <i>The Spectrum</i> is the only independent publication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bullstory_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bullstory-124">[123]</a></sup> <i>Generation</i> is funded by advertising and through Sub-Board I,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> the student services corporation. UB also has a student radio station, WRUB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> WRUB broadcasts all UB home football games and select road games, as well as most UB men's and women's home basketball games.</p>
<p>After the retirement of <a href="/wiki/John_B._Simpson" title="John B. Simpson">John B. Simpson</a>, the undergraduate students have also developed a university forum<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> with the hopes of developing a thriving online campus. This move was supported by now incumbent president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satish_K_Tripathi" title="Satish K Tripathi">Satish K Tripathi</a> who called it a "model of University spirit and entrepreneurship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UB Student Alumni Association (UBSAA) annually hosts the world's largest collegiate mud-volleyball game known as "Oozefest". 192 teams of at least six students compete in a double elimination volleyball tournament at "The Mud Pit" each Spring before finals. Fire trucks are brought in to saturate the dirt courts to create the mud. Awards are handed out to not only the victors, but the most creatively dressed. In the past, students have worn business suits and even dresses to the tournament.</p>
<p>Held annually since 1991 has been the Linda Yalem Safety Run, formerly called the Linda Yalem Memorial Run. Linda Yalem was a sophomore at UB who was studying communications and training for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Marathon" title="New York City Marathon">New York City Marathon</a> when she was raped and killed by <a href="/wiki/Altemio_Sanchez" title="Altemio Sanchez">Altemio Sanchez</a> after going for a run on the <a href="/wiki/Ellicott_Creek_Bike_Path" title="Ellicott Creek Bike Path">Ellicott Creek Bike Path</a> on September 29, 1990. The Run is held every year in her memory and to promote safety for runners.</p>
<p>In 1923, an honorary senior society called Bisonhead was founded. It has since represented twelve undergraduate leaders at UB each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spectrum_article_on_Bisonhead_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spectrum_article_on_Bisonhead-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of UB's clubs are run through the Undergraduate Student Association and the Graduate Student Association, with each level requiring respective senate recognition for clubs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg/240px-LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg/360px-LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg/480px-LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LakelasalleUBnorth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lake LaSalle and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Greiner" title="Bill Greiner">Greiner</a> Hall behind the Ellicott Complex</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UB_Ellicott_Complex,_May_1992.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="841" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg/220px-UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg/330px-UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg/440px-UB_Ellicott_Complex%2C_May_1992.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UB_Ellicott_Complex,_May_1992.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Partial view of UB Ellicott Complex, May 1992</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Student residence halls are located on both the North and South Campuses. On the North Campus, there is the Ellicott Complex, which consists of Fargo, Porter, Red Jacket, Richmond, Spaulding, and Wilkeson Quadrangles. The Ellicott Complex is also known as "Lego Land" because the shapes of the buildings resemble Legos stacked upon each other. Next to Fargo Quad is the newly built in 2011 <a href="/wiki/Bill_Greiner" title="Bill Greiner">Greiner</a> Hall, a dorm strictly for sophomores. Also on North Campus is the Governors Complex, home to the Freshman Honors Housing and various other living communities. There are also off-campus housing options close to the north campus such as The Triad Apartments.</p>
<p>On South Campus is Goodyear and Clement Hall. The unique aspect of these dorms is that residents share a bathroom with the adjacent room, rather than have a communal bathroom. Up until Spring of 2011, there were four other dorm buildings, referred to as "The Quad": MacDonald, Pritchard, Schoellkopf, and Michael Hall. Michael Hall currently exists as the Student Health Center, the other three are not in use.</p>
<p>In 1999, the university built its first apartment complex for families and graduate students at Flickinger Court. Since the success of Flickinger, UB has developed South Lake Village, Hadley Village, Flint Village, and Creekside Apartments. Most students who wish to still live on or near the North Campus but enjoy the lifestyle of apartment living take advantage of these apartments. University Village at Sweethome, Villas at Rensch, and Villas at Chestnut Ridge are student apartment communities adjacent to the North Campus and offer a shuttle service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> Collegiate Village off campus apartments offers transportation to both North and South Campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> Students also find housing in private locations. Those locations are generally situated in the University Heights district of Buffalo, and other areas close to the North and South Campuses. The school assigns rooms based on a lottery system.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bulls" title="Buffalo Bulls">Buffalo Bulls</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victor_E._Bull,_November_5,_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg/225px-Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg/338px-Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg/450px-Victor_E._Bull%2C_November_5%2C_2013.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victor_E._Bull,_November_5,_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Victor_E._Bull" title="Victor E. Bull">Victor E. Bull</a>, November 5, 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The school's sports teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bulls" title="Buffalo Bulls">Buffalo Bulls</a>, or UB Bulls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> The women's teams were originally called the Buffalo Royals. The Bulls currently play in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="Football Bowl Subdivision">Division I FBS</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> in <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> and are a member of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">Mid-American Conference</a> (MAC) for all sports except women's rowing, which is in the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a> (CAA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> The Bulls have been a member of the Mid-American Conference since 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Division_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Division-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Buffalo Bulls field 11 men's and women's athletic teams in sports, although only nine team sports for both men and women are identified on the official website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-4"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> Men's team sports at UB include those in football, basketball, track and field, baseball, wrestling, soccer, swimming and diving, cross country, and tennis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-5"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> The Bulls' women's teams feature basketball, track and field, cross country, volleyball, softball, soccer, rowing, tennis, and swimming and diving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulls_132-6"><a href="#cite_note-Bulls-132">[131]</a></sup> Cheerleading is co-ed. The Bulls have had dozens of athletes turn professional in football, baseball, basketball, soccer, and volleyball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pros_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pros-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mascot of UB's athletic teams is <a href="/wiki/Victor_E._Bull" title="Victor E. Bull">Victor E. Bull</a>, a blue bull with a gold nose ring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Victor_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Victor-135">[134]</a></sup> The university is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thunder_of_the_East" title="Thunder of the East">Thunder of the East</a> marching band. The band performs at all home football games and travels to both local and national parades and competitions. Buffalo has three fight songs: "Victory March", "Go for a Touchdown", and "Buffalo Fight Song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2005 the men's basketball team reached the Mid-American Conference Championship game, but lost 79–80 to the Ohio Bobcats, thus missing a chance for their first trip to the NCAA Tournament. In 2015 the bulls won their conference championship game, and won the MAC Tournament, making their first trip to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a>. In 2016 the men's basketball team once again won the MAC championship game, making their second trip to the NCAA Tournament in a row. The women's basketball team also won the MAC and made their first trip to the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a> in program history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rowing program is an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a>. The Women's Rowing team won the CAA championship in April 2010 for the first time. In May 2010, the team won the Jack &amp; Nancy Seitz Women's Point Trophy at the Dad Vail Regatta for the third year in a row. In 2015 UB's men track and field star, Jonathan Jones, became the first national champion in UB's Division I history when he won the shot put at the NCAA Outdoor Track and Field Championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1958, the football team won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lambert_Cup" title="Lambert Cup">Lambert Cup</a>, emblematic of supremacy in Eastern U.S. small-college football. That led to the team's first bowl invitation, to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangerine_Bowl_(1947%E2%80%9382)" title="Tangerine Bowl (1947–82)">Tangerine Bowl</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a>. But the Bulls would be allowed to participate only if backup defensive end Mike Wilson and starting halfback <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willie_R._Evans_(running_back)" title="Willie R. Evans (running back)">Willie Evans</a>, who were black, did not play. The team stood behind the two, and refused the bowl offer; Buffalo did not receive another bowl invitation until the 2008 season when they won the <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">MAC</a> championship against previously undefeated <a href="/wiki/Ball_State_University" title="Ball State University">Ball State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several UB football stars from the 1950s and early 1960s went on to play professional football, including quarterback <a href="/wiki/John_Stofa" title="John Stofa">John Stofa</a> with the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>, and defensive lineman <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Philbin" title="Gerry Philbin">Gerry Philbin</a> with the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">AFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>. Philbin is a member of the AFL Hall of Fame and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-time_All-AFL_Team" title="All-time All-AFL Team">All-time All-AFL Team</a>. Philbin and UB's Willie Ross were the first two UB graduates to play on professional football championship teams in the United States: Ross with the 1964 AFL Champion <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a>; and Philbin with the 1968 AFL Champion <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, who also won that season's <a href="/wiki/Professional_American_football_championship_games" title="Professional American football championship games">AFL-NFL World Championship Game</a> (Super Bowl III). <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a> was on the Green Bay Packers Super Bowl XLV champions as a rookie. <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Guzman" title="Ramon Guzman">Ramon Guzman</a> played on the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Grey_Cup" title="Grey Cup">Grey Cup</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Mack" title="Khalil Mack">Khalil Mack</a> was selected as the 1st round 5th pick in the NFL draft, becoming Buffalo's first, first round draft pick. <a href="/wiki/Branden_Oliver" title="Branden Oliver">Branden Oliver</a> has also risen to fame in the 2014 season as the running back for the Chargers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_at_Buffalo_people" title="List of University at Buffalo people">List of University at Buffalo people</a></div>
<p>UB hails over 230,000 alumni who live in over 130 countries in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> Among the individuals who have attended, graduated, or taught at the University are <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> astronaut <a href="/wiki/Ellen_S._Baker" title="Ellen S. Baker">Ellen S. Baker</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emmy" title="Emmy">Emmy</a>-winning American journalist <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Blitzer" title="Wolf Blitzer">Wolf Blitzer</a>, Chairman and former CEO of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%2BE_Networks" title="A+E Networks">A+E Networks</a> <a href="/wiki/Abbe_Raven" title="Abbe Raven">Abbe Raven</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> <a href="/wiki/Brad_Grey" title="Brad Grey">Brad Grey</a>, billionaire and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a> <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a>, Pulitzer Prize-winner <a href="/wiki/Tom_Toles" title="Tom Toles">Tom Toles</a>, Nobel Prize-winners, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Coase" title="Ronald Coase">Ronald Coase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_A._Hauptman" title="Herbert A. Hauptman">Herbert A. Hauptman</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_John_Carew_Eccles" title="Sir John Carew Eccles">Sir John Carew Eccles</a>, and winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology_and_Innovation" title="National Medal of Technology and Innovation">National Medal of Technology and Innovation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_McCombs" title="Norman McCombs">Norman McCombs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilson_Greatbach" title="Wilson Greatbach">Wilson Greatbach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Erich_Bloch" title="Erich Bloch">Erich Bloch</a>. Billionaire and owner of the Boston Bruins, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jacobs" title="Jeremy Jacobs">Jeremy Jacobs</a>, musician and civil rights activist <a href="/wiki/Charles_Mingus" title="Charles Mingus">Charles Mingus</a>, pianist and composer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Aaker_Trythall" title="Richard Aaker Trythall">Richard Aaker Trythall</a>, civil engineer, genealogist and author <a href="/wiki/Angelo_F._Coniglio" title="Angelo F. Coniglio">Angelo F. Coniglio</a>, scholar of medieval religion <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Muessig" title="Carolyn Muessig">Carolyn Muessig</a>, and American actor, director, and producer <a href="/wiki/Ron_Silver" title="Ron Silver">Ron Silver</a>. Amongst the athletes who have graduated from the University are football players <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Philbin" title="Gerry Philbin">Gerry Philbin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naaman_Roosevelt" title="Naaman Roosevelt">Naaman Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branden_Oliver" title="Branden Oliver">Branden Oliver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Mack" title="Khalil Mack">Khalil Mack</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a> along with soccer player <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Shuttleworth" title="Bobby Shuttleworth">Bobby Shuttleworth</a>.</p>
<p>Over the years, the University at Buffalo has also been particularly distinguished in contemporary creative writing. Noted novelists who have taught on its faculty include <a href="/wiki/John_Barth" title="John Barth">John Barth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Federman" title="Raymond Federman">Raymond Federman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Burgess" title="Anthony Burgess">Anthony Burgess</a>. Noted faculty poets include George Starbuck (1983 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize">Lenore Marshall Prize</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Olson" title="Charles Olson">Charles Olson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Creeley" title="Robert Creeley">Robert Creeley</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bollingen_Prize" title="Bollingen Prize">Bollingen Prize</a> 1999), <a href="/wiki/John_Logan_(poet)" title="John Logan (poet)">John Logan</a>, (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize">Lenore Marshall Prize</a> 1982), <a href="/wiki/Irving_Feldman" title="Irving Feldman">Irving Feldman</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MacArthur_Foundation_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Foundation Fellowship">MacArthur Foundation Fellow</a> 1992), <a href="/wiki/Carl_Dennis" title="Carl Dennis">Carl Dennis</a> (2000 <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Lilly_Poetry_Prize" title="Ruth Lilly Poetry Prize">Ruth Lilly Poetry Prize</a>; 2002 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Poetry" title="Pulitzer Prize for Poetry">Pulitzer Prize for Poetry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hass" title="Robert Hass">Robert Hass</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate_of_the_United_States" title="Poet Laureate of the United States">Poet Laureate of the United States</a> 1995–97, 2007 <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Award" title="National Book Award">National Book Award</a>, 2008 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Poetry" title="Pulitzer Prize for Poetry">Pulitzer Prize for Poetry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bernstein" title="Charles Bernstein">Charles Bernstein</a> (co-founder of the University's notable Poetics Program), <a href="/wiki/Steve_McCaffery" title="Steve McCaffery">Steve McCaffery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Susan_Howe" title="Susan Howe">Susan Howe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bollingen_Prize" title="Bollingen Prize">Bollingen Prize</a> 2011). Former UB students include Michael Casey (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yale_Younger_Poets_Award" title="Yale Younger Poets Award">Yale Younger Poets Award</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Petrosky" title="Anthony Petrosky">Tony Petrosky</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walt_Whitman_Award" title="Walt Whitman Award">Walt Whitman Award</a>), <a href="/wiki/Donald_Revell" title="Donald Revell">Donald Revell</a> (2004 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize">Lenore Marshall Prize</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Baxter_(author)" title="Charles Baxter (author)">Charles Baxter</a>, Michael Davidson, and, from the Poetics Program, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Willis" title="Elizabeth Willis">Elizabeth Willis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gizzi" title="Peter Gizzi">Peter Gizzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juliana_Spahr" title="Juliana Spahr">Juliana Spahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jena_Osman" title="Jena Osman">Jena Osman</a>, and Yunte Huang.</p>
<p>Political leaders who have attended and taught at the University include the 13th President of the United States and 12th Vice President of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>, the 21st Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Abdullahi_Mohamed" title="Mohamed Abdullahi Mohamed">Mohamed Abdullahi Mohamed</a>, and the Minister of Education of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Ji" title="Zhou Ji">Zhou Ji</a>. Alumni have also served in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, including former Congress Members <a href="/wiki/Jack_Quinn_(politician)" title="Jack Quinn (politician)">Jack Quinn</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Congressbio_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Congressbio-141">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quinn_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quinn-142">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campaigns_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campaigns-143">[142]</a></sup> and the late <a href="/wiki/William_F._Walsh" title="William F. Walsh">William F. Walsh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walsh_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walsh-144">[143]</a></sup> Other lawmakers, such as <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Assembly" title="New York State Assembly">New York State Assembly</a> Member <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Giglio" title="Joseph Giglio">Joseph Giglio</a> and former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State_Attorney_General" title="New York State Attorney General">New York State Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Vacco" title="Dennis Vacco">Dennis Vacco</a>, are also UB graduates.</p>

<li id="cite_note-Hough-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Hough_12-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hough_12-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hough_12-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Hough, Franklin B., M.
